  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_9f603a4a-edd3-4411-bcbb-6b828faf103c'
      });

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer18090727587268512924"><b>Find here the original trilogy from Anne Rice's bestselling series about the lives of Mayfair witches...</b><br/><br/><br/><b>The Witching Hour</b><br/>Demonstrating once again her gift for spellbinding storytelling, Anne Rice makes real for us a great dynasty of four centuries of witches--a family given to poetry and incest, murder and philosophy, a family that over the ages is itself haunted by a powe</span>
  <span id="freeText18090727587268512924" style="display:none"><b>Find here the original trilogy from Anne Rice's bestselling series about the lives of Mayfair witches...</b><br /><br /><br /><b>The Witching Hour</b><br />Demonstrating once again her gift for spellbinding storytelling, Anne Rice makes real for us a great dynasty of four centuries of witches--a family given to poetry and incest, murder and philosophy, a family that over the ages is itself haunted by a powerful, dangerous, and seductive being called Lasher who haunts the Mayfair women...<br /><br /><b>Lasher</b><br />At the center of this novel: the brilliant and beautiful Rowan Mayfair, queen of the coven -- and Lasher, the darkly compelling demon whom she finds irresistible and from whose evil spell and vision she must now flee.  She takes with her their terrifying and exquisite child, one of "a brood of children born knowing, able to stand and talk on the first day." Rowan's attempt to escape Lasher and his pursuit of her and their child are at the heart of this extraordinary saga, moving around the globe, backward and forward through time, and between the human and demonic worlds...<br /><br /><b>Taltos</b><br />Ashlar is the last of his race--or so he thinks. When he learns that another Taltos has been seen, he is suddenly propelled into the haunting world of the Mayfair family, the New Orleans dynasty of witches forever besieged by ghosts, spirits, and their own dizzying powers. For Ashlar knows this powerful clan is intimately linked to the heritage of the Taltos. This mesmerizing novel takes us on a wondrous journey back through the centuries to a civilization half-human, of wholly mysterious origin, at odds with mortality and immortality, justice and guilt. It is an enchanted, hypnotic world that could only come from the imagination of Anne Rice...</span>
  <a data-text-id="18090727587268512924" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1139393049" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1139393049" />
    <a title="Laurie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12251589-laurie"><img alt="Laurie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1396010679p2/12251589.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1139393049?book_show_action=true">Dec 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laurie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laurie" href="/user/show/12251589-laurie">Laurie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18874332-the-mayfair-witches-series-3-book-bundle">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1139393049" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12396144073471896543">This was actually my second time through all three of these. Having just picked up "The Prince Lestat", I realized it has been a very loooong time since I read much of Rice's stuff and I'd forgotten a number of salient points. So I began backtracking. That led me to Vampire Chronicles #7: Merrick. Merrick was a Mayfair. Not from the main branch of the family, but as we learned with Mayfairs, that is seldom reason to assume ANY Mayfair lacks "gifts".<br/><br/>I quickly realized how interconnected all of he</span>
  <span id="freeText12396144073471896543" style="display:none">This was actually my second time through all three of these. Having just picked up "The Prince Lestat", I realized it has been a very loooong time since I read much of Rice's stuff and I'd forgotten a number of salient points. So I began backtracking. That led me to Vampire Chronicles #7: Merrick. Merrick was a Mayfair. Not from the main branch of the family, but as we learned with Mayfairs, that is seldom reason to assume ANY Mayfair lacks "gifts".<br /><br />I quickly realized how interconnected all of her Vampire Chronicles and the Mayfair Witches stories are! So back I went to reread all of the Mayfair Witches series.<br /><br />I'm glad I did. I picked up on much that I'd missed the first time around with both The Witching Hour and Lasher. I'm about halfway through Lasher now. If you haven't read these in the past decade or more, and you liked them the first time around, you might wish to revisit them. As with all gifted authors and great stories, what you take away from a story changes perspective at different points in your life. I'm now in my mid-fifties and I find myself empathizing more, and paying more attention, to the older characters. As a result, I'm taking away an entirely different perspective.<br /><br />This is every bit as much a grand Southern Gothic novel as much as a Gothic Horror novel. I missed that the first time around when I was in my early 30s. I find myself seeing the broader canvas upon which the actions of the players are painted, not simply zooming ahead with the actions of the key participants.<br /><br />It's not a set of novels I would have expected to stand the test of time, but they hold up remarkably well. I find myself pleasantly surprised and thrilled to be wrong.<br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="12396144073471896543" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2177778536" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2177778536?book_show_action=true">Apr 17, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="M.M. Strawberry Library &amp; Reviews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="M.M. Strawberry Library &amp; Reviews" href="/user/show/12558730-m-m-strawberry-library-reviews">M.M. Strawberry Library &amp; Reviews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12558730-m-m-strawberry-library-reviews?shelf=author-anne-rice">author-anne-rice</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12558730-m-m-strawberry-library-reviews?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12558730-m-m-strawberry-library-reviews?shelf=family-saga">family-saga</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12558730-m-m-strawberry-library-reviews?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12558730-m-m-strawberry-library-reviews?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12558730-m-m-strawberry-library-reviews?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2177778536" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14874094330618939714">I have mixed feelings about this series as a whole. The first book was very solid, especially with the file the Talamasca had on the Mayfairs, it made for a well-rounded story, and remains one of my favorite of Anne Rice's novels. The ending absolutely leaves one in suspense and eager to read the next book to see what happens.<br/><br/>Unfortunately, Lasher turns out to be a huge rape-feat. He ties up Rowan and rapes her repeatedly, desperate to start a new race of Taltos, heedless of the effect that this</span>
  <span id="freeText14874094330618939714" style="display:none">I have mixed feelings about this series as a whole. The first book was very solid, especially with the file the Talamasca had on the Mayfairs, it made for a well-rounded story, and remains one of my favorite of Anne Rice's novels. The ending absolutely leaves one in suspense and eager to read the next book to see what happens.<br /><br />Unfortunately, Lasher turns out to be a huge rape-feat. He ties up Rowan and rapes her repeatedly, desperate to start a new race of Taltos, heedless of the effect that this has on her health. Aside from learning more about the Mayfair Witches and Lasher through backstory narratives, this book didn't add much to the world of the Mayfair Witches.<br /><br />Taltos was a little better, and we learn some substantial information about the Taltos, but the first book in this series remains the strongest one. The whole series could have been so much better had Ms. Rice went into different directions with several of the plot points of Lasher/Taltos.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14874094330618939714" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Ramona" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12211001-ramona"><img alt="Ramona" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1348610556p2/12211001.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1314822124" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4262364685598911991">I should include a caveat that I only listened to the abridged audiobook set of these books (not realizing that the only Audible audiobooks for the series were abridged).<br/><br/>That caveat aside, definitely not my thing. I love fantasy and mystery and magic and even the occassional lascivious or libidinous description of a romantic encounter. But this book went too far, got too weird, and was too unsettling - and not in a "wow, I'm really getting lost in this dark and mysterious world and am experienci</span>
  <span id="freeText4262364685598911991" style="display:none">I should include a caveat that I only listened to the abridged audiobook set of these books (not realizing that the only Audible audiobooks for the series were abridged).<br /><br />That caveat aside, definitely not my thing. I love fantasy and mystery and magic and even the occassional lascivious or libidinous description of a romantic encounter. But this book went too far, got too weird, and was too unsettling - and not in a "wow, I'm really getting lost in this dark and mysterious world and am experiencing disturbing emotions" kind of way (which can actually be the hallmark of really great writing to me) - more of an "ick, what am I reading, and what is going on, and who are all those people, and just ick" kind of way.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4262364685598911991" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3011538649?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="William" class="user" itemprop="url" name="William" href="/user/show/62104280-william">William</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio Cassette 9780375416200" href="/book/show/43819.Anne_Rice_Value_Collection">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3011538649" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14446523882291923470">I have tried to enjoy Anne Rice, but the stories are long and boring. Nowhere on this audiobook did it say abridged. I don’t normally read abridged works. But normally abridge works cut out the unnecessary boring bits. If that is true id’ of never of made it thought the full text. This was drawn out difficult to follow. The history of a family is not interesting. It might be what I would write for myself to as backstory for a character, but never would I publish it. I can’t image what agent read</span>
  <span id="freeText14446523882291923470" style="display:none">I have tried to enjoy Anne Rice, but the stories are long and boring. Nowhere on this audiobook did it say abridged. I don’t normally read abridged works. But normally abridge works cut out the unnecessary boring bits. If that is true id’ of never of made it thought the full text. This was drawn out difficult to follow. The history of a family is not interesting. It might be what I would write for myself to as backstory for a character, but never would I publish it. I can’t image what agent read this and said yes this the next great published work. It really is just a snore fest. I only finished it so I could count it towards my reading goal. So many people recommend her for dark tails including her vampire stories but they do nothing for me as a reader. They are slow and lack any action to drive the story forward. They almost read as if following a person on a day to day life and that is boring. Hit the exciting bits and maybe a little less breast milk fetishes. </span>
  <a data-text-id="14446523882291923470" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('+xrUX1fkJb0U1AjVxBOPaSOEoObUHSYJBYrX+wS/s7dPDDidrGh9AgvpMYb4tqGsqczgG6GsaaT5WH1yy/yELg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

The diary not only follows the development of a girl into womanhood, it follows the construction of the Rimbauer mansion—called Rose Red—an enormous home that would be the site of so many horrific and inexplicable tragedies in the years ahead.\n\nThe Diary of Ellen Rimbauer: My Life at Rose Red is a rare document, one that gives us an unusual view of daily life among the aristocracy in the early 1900s, a window into one woman\'s hidden emotional torment, and a record of the mysterious events at Rose Red that scandalized Seattle society at the time—events that can only be fully understood now that the diary has come to light. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer959672137228764427">Anne Rice (born Howard Allen Frances O'Brien) is a best-selling American author of gothic, supernatural, historical, erotica, and later religious themed books. Best known for <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/search?utf8=%E2%9C%93&query=The+Vampire+Chronicles' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Vampire Chronicles</a>, her prevailing thematical focus is on love, death, immortality, existentialism, and the human condition. She was married to poet <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/222961.Stan_Rice' title='Stan Rice' rel='nofollow noopener'>Stan Rice</a> for 41 years until his death in 2002. Her books have sold near</span>
  <span id="freeText959672137228764427" style="display:none">Anne Rice (born Howard Allen Frances O'Brien) is a best-selling American author of gothic, supernatural, historical, erotica, and later religious themed books. Best known for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/search?utf8=%E2%9C%93&amp;query=The+Vampire+Chronicles" rel="nofollow noopener">The Vampire Chronicles</a>, her prevailing thematical focus is on love, death, immortality, existentialism, and the human condition. She was married to poet <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/222961.Stan_Rice" title="Stan Rice" rel="nofollow noopener">Stan Rice</a> for 41 years until his death in 2002. Her books have sold nearly 100 million copies, making her one of the most widely read authors in modern history.<br /><br />She uses the pseudonym <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/17553.Anne_Rampling" rel="nofollow noopener">Anne Rampling</a> for adult-themed fiction (i.e., erotica) and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/437669.A_N_Roquelaure" rel="nofollow noopener">A.N. Roquelaure</a> for fiction featuring sexually explicit sado-masochism.</span>

      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_11901'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11901.The_Witching_Hour?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">The Witching Hour (Lives of the Mayfair Witches, #1)<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/7577.Anne_Rice?origin=series_works\">Anne Rice<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.11 avg rating &mdash; 102,522 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 1990\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer6319974298749254195\">From the author of the extraordinary Vampire Chronicles comes a huge, hypnotic novel of witchcraft and the occult through four centuries.\n\nDemonstrating, once again, her gift for spellbinding storytelling and the creation of legend, Anne Rice makes r<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText6319974298749254195\" style=\"display:none\">From the author of the extraordinary Vampire Chronicles comes a huge, hypnotic novel of witchcraft and the occult through four centuries.\n\nDemonstrating, once again, her gift for spellbinding storytelling and the creation of legend, Anne Rice makes real for us a great dynasty of witches—a family given to poetry and to incest, to murder and to philosophy; a family that, over the ages, is itself haunted by a powerful, dangerous, and seductive being.\n\nOn the veranda of a great New Orleans house, now faded, a mute and fragile woman sits rocking... and The Witching Hour begins.\n\nIt begins in our time with a rescue at sea.  Rowan Mayfair, a beautiful woman, a brilliant practitioner of neurosurgery—aware that she has special powers but unaware that she comes from an ancient line of witches—finds the drowned body of a man off the coast of California and brings him to life.  He is Michael Curry, who was born in New Orleans and orphaned in childhood by fire on Christmas Eve, who pulled himself up from poverty, and who now, in his brief interval of death, has acquired a sensory power that mystifies and frightens him.\n\nAs these two, fiercely drawn to each other, fall in love and—in passionate alliance—set out to solve the mystery of her past and his unwelcome gift, the novel moves backward and forward in time from today\'s New Orleans and San Francisco to long-ago Amsterdam and a château in the France of Louis XIV.  An intricate tale of evil unfolds—an evil unleashed in seventeenth-century Scotland, where the first &quot;witch,&quot; Suzanne of the Mayfair, conjures up the spirit she names Lasher... a creation that spells her own destruction and torments each of her descendants in turn.\n\nFrom the coffee plantations of Port au Prince, where the great Mayfair fortune is made and the legacy of their dark power is almost destroyed, to Civil War New Orleans, as Julien—the clan\'s only male to be endowed with occult powers—provides for the dynasty its foothold in America, the dark, luminous story encompasses dramas of seduction and death, episodes of tenderness and healing.  And always—through peril and escape, tension and release—there swirl around us the echoes of eternal war: innocence versus the corruption of the spirit, sanity against madness, life against death.  With a dreamlike power, the novel draws us, through circuitous, twilight paths, to the present and Rowan\'s increasingly inspired and risky moves in the merciless game that binds her to her heritage. And in New Orleans, on Christmas Eve, this strangest of family sagas is brought to its startling climax.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"6319974298749254195\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));;
